        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Electric_car_diagram.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Electric_car_diagram.svg/220px-Electric_car_diagram.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Electric_car_diagram.svg/330px-Electric_car_diagram.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Electric_car_diagram.svg/440px-Electric_car_diagram.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="287"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Electric_car_diagram.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Low battery and motors can improve safety<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Alternative_fuel_vehicle" title="Alternative fuel vehicle">Alternative fuel vehicle</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The transport sector is a major contributor to <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air pollution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Noise_pollution" title="Noise pollution">noise pollution</a> and <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Most cars in use in the early 2020s run on <a href="/wiki/Gasoline" title="Gasoline">gasoline</a> burnt in an <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">internal combustion engine</a> (ICE). The <a href="/wiki/Organisation_Internationale_des_Constructeurs_d%27Automobiles" title="Organisation Internationale des Constructeurs d'Automobiles">International Organization of Motor Vehicle Manufacturers</a> says that, in countries that mandate low sulfur gasoline, gasoline-fuelled cars built to late 2010s standards (such as Euro-6) emit very little local air pollution.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Some cities ban older gasoline-fuelled cars and some countries plan to ban sales in future. However some environmental groups say this <a href="/wiki/Phase-out_of_fossil_fuel_vehicles" title="Phase-out of fossil fuel vehicles">phase-out of fossil fuel vehicles</a> must be brought forward to limit climate change. Production of gasoline fueled cars peaked in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-IEA2019_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IEA2019-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Other hydrocarbon fossil fuels also burnt by <a href="/wiki/Deflagration" title="Deflagration">deflagration</a> (rather than <a href="/wiki/Detonation" title="Detonation">detonation</a>) in ICE cars include <a href="/wiki/Diesel_fuel" title="Diesel fuel">diesel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Autogas" title="Autogas">Autogas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Compressed_natural_gas" title="Compressed natural gas">CNG</a>. Removal of <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_subsidies" title="Fossil fuel subsidies">fossil fuel subsidies</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> concerns about <a href="/wiki/Energy_security" title="Energy security">oil dependence</a>, tightening <a href="/wiki/Environmental_law" title="Environmental law">environmental laws</a> and restrictions on <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions" title="Greenhouse gas emissions">greenhouse gas emissions</a> are propelling work on alternative power systems for cars. This includes <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_vehicle" title="Hybrid vehicle">hybrid vehicles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicle" title="Plug-in electric vehicle">plug-in electric vehicles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_vehicle" title="Hydrogen vehicle">hydrogen vehicles</a>. Out of all cars sold in 2020, 4.6% were plug-in electric, and by the end of that year there were more than 10 million <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_car" class="mw-redirect" title="Plug-in electric car">plug-in electric cars</a> on the world's roads.<sup id="cite_ref-:12_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-49">[49]</a></sup> Despite rapid growth, only about 1% of cars on the world's roads were <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_vehicle" title="Battery electric vehicle">fully electric</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrid</a> cars by the end of 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-:12_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-49">[49]</a></sup> Cars for racing or <a href="/wiki/Land_speed_record" title="Land speed record">speed records</a> have sometimes employed <a href="/wiki/Jet_car" title="Jet car">jet</a> or <a href="/wiki/Rocket_car" title="Rocket car">rocket</a> engines, but these are impractical for common use. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Oil_consumption" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil consumption">Oil consumption</a> has increased rapidly in the 20th and 21st centuries because there are more cars; the <a href="/wiki/1980s_oil_glut" title="1980s oil glut">1985–2003 oil glut</a> even fuelled the sales of low-economy vehicles in <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a> countries. The <a href="/wiki/BRIC" title="BRIC">BRIC</a> countries are adding to this consumption. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="User_interface">User interface</span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:1923_Ford_Model_T_UPS_interior.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/1923_Ford_Model_T_UPS_interior.jpg/220px-1923_Ford_Model_T_UPS_interior.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/1923_Ford_Model_T_UPS_interior.jpg/330px-1923_Ford_Model_T_UPS_interior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/1923_Ford_Model_T_UPS_interior.jpg/440px-1923_Ford_Model_T_UPS_interior.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:1923_Ford_Model_T_UPS_interior.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>In the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Model_T" title="Ford Model T">Ford Model T</a> the left-side hand lever sets the rear wheel parking brakes and puts the transmission in neutral. The lever to the right controls the throttle. The lever on the left of the steering column is for ignition timing. The left foot pedal changes the two forward gears while the centre pedal controls reverse. The right pedal is the brake.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Car_controls" title="Car controls">Car controls</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Cars are equipped with controls used for driving, passenger comfort, and safety, normally operated by a combination of the use of feet and hands, and occasionally by voice on 21st-century cars. These controls include a <a href="/wiki/Steering_wheel" title="Steering wheel">steering wheel</a>, pedals for operating the brakes and controlling the car's speed (and, in a manual transmission car, a clutch pedal), a shift lever or stick for changing gears, and a number of buttons and dials for turning on lights, ventilation, and other functions. Modern cars' controls are now standardized, such as the location for the accelerator and brake, but this was not always the case. Controls are evolving in response to new technologies, for example, the <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">electric car</a> and the integration of mobile communications. </p>
      <p>Some of the original controls are no longer required. For example, all cars once had controls for the choke valve, clutch, <a href="/wiki/Ignition_timing" title="Ignition timing">ignition timing</a>, and a crank instead of an electric <a href="/wiki/Starter_(engine)" title="Starter (engine)">starter</a>. However new controls have also been added to vehicles, making them more complex. These include <a href="/wiki/Automobile_air_conditioning" title="Automobile air conditioning">air conditioning</a>, <a href="/wiki/Automotive_navigation_system" title="Automotive navigation system">navigation systems</a>, and <a href="/wiki/In_car_entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="In car entertainment">in car entertainment</a>. Another trend is the replacement of physical knobs and switches by secondary controls with touchscreen controls such as <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMW</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/IDrive" title="IDrive">iDrive</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company" title="Ford Motor Company">Ford</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/MyFord_Touch" title="MyFord Touch">MyFord Touch</a></i>. Another change is that while early cars' pedals were physically linked to the brake mechanism and throttle, in the early 2020s, cars have increasingly replaced these physical linkages with electronic controls. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Electronics_and_interior">Electronics and interior</span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Blade_fuses_on_Citroen_Jumper.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Blade_fuses_on_Citroen_Jumper.JPG/220px-Blade_fuses_on_Citroen_Jumper.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Blade_fuses_on_Citroen_Jumper.JPG/330px-Blade_fuses_on_Citroen_Jumper.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Blade_fuses_on_Citroen_Jumper.JPG/440px-Blade_fuses_on_Citroen_Jumper.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2056"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Blade_fuses_on_Citroen_Jumper.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Fuse_(automotive)#Mount" title="Fuse (automotive)">Panel</a> for fuses and circuit breakers
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Cars are typically equipped with interior lighting which can be toggled manually or be set to light up with automatically doors open, an <a href="/wiki/In-car_entertainment" title="In-car entertainment">entertainment system</a> which originated from <a href="/wiki/Car_radio" class="mw-redirect" title="Car radio">car radios</a>, sideways <a href="/wiki/Car_window" class="mw-redirect" title="Car window">windows</a> which can be lowered or raised electrically (manually on earlier cars), and one or multiple <a href="/wiki/Automobile_auxiliary_power_outlet" title="Automobile auxiliary power outlet">auxiliary power outlets</a> for supplying portable appliances such as <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone_charger" class="mw-redirect" title="Mobile phone charger">mobile phones</a>, portable fridges, <a href="/wiki/Power_inverter" title="Power inverter">power inverters</a>, and electrical air pumps from the on-board electrical system.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[a]</a></sup> More costly upper-class and <a href="/wiki/Luxury_car" title="Luxury car">luxury cars</a> are equipped with features earlier such as massage seats and <a href="/wiki/Collision_avoidance_system" title="Collision avoidance system">collision avoidance systems</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Fuse_(automotive)" title="Fuse (automotive)">Dedicated automotive fuses and circuit breakers</a> prevent damage from <a href="/wiki/Electrical_overload" class="mw-redirect" title="Electrical overload">electrical overload</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Lighting">Lighting</span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:LED_DaytimeRunningLights.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/LED_DaytimeRunningLights.jpg/220px-LED_DaytimeRunningLights.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/LED_DaytimeRunningLights.jpg/330px-LED_DaytimeRunningLights.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/LED_DaytimeRunningLights.jpg/440px-LED_DaytimeRunningLights.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3526" data-file-height="2350"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:LED_DaytimeRunningLights.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Audi_A4" title="Audi A4">Audi A4</a> <a href="/wiki/Daytime_running_lights" class="mw-redirect" title="Daytime running lights">daytime running lights</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Automotive_lighting" title="Automotive lighting">Automotive lighting</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Cars are typically fitted with multiple types of lights. These include <a href="/wiki/Headlight" class="mw-redirect" title="Headlight">headlights</a>, which are used to illuminate the way ahead and make the car visible to other users, so that the vehicle can be used at night; in some jurisdictions, <a href="/wiki/Daytime_running_lights" class="mw-redirect" title="Daytime running lights">daytime running lights</a>; red brake lights to indicate when the brakes are applied; amber turn signal lights to indicate the turn intentions of the driver; white-colored reverse lights to illuminate the area behind the car (and indicate that the driver will be or is reversing); and on some vehicles, additional lights (e.g., side marker lights) to increase the visibility of the car. Interior lights on the ceiling of the car are usually fitted for the driver and passengers. Some vehicles also have a trunk light and, more rarely, an engine compartment light. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Weight">Weight</span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Smart_Fortwo_passion_front.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Smart_Fortwo_passion_front.JPG/220px-Smart_Fortwo_passion_front.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Smart_Fortwo_passion_front.JPG/330px-Smart_Fortwo_passion_front.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Smart_Fortwo_passion_front.JPG/440px-Smart_Fortwo_passion_front.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2295" data-file-height="1740"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Smart_Fortwo_passion_front.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Smart_Fortwo" title="Smart Fortwo">Smart Fortwo</a> car from 1998 to 2002, weighing 730&nbsp;kg (1,610&nbsp;lb)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:07-08_Chevrolet_Suburban_LT.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/07-08_Chevrolet_Suburban_LT.jpg/220px-07-08_Chevrolet_Suburban_LT.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/07-08_Chevrolet_Suburban_LT.jpg/330px-07-08_Chevrolet_Suburban_LT.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/07-08_Chevrolet_Suburban_LT.jpg/440px-07-08_Chevrolet_Suburban_LT.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1989" data-file-height="1140"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:07-08_Chevrolet_Suburban_LT.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Suburban" title="Chevrolet Suburban">Chevrolet Suburban</a> extended-length SUV weighs 3,300&nbsp;kg (7,200&nbsp;lb) (gross weight)<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During the late 20th and early 21st century cars increased in weight due to batteries,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup> modern steel safety cages, anti-lock brakes, airbags, and "more-powerful—if more-efficient—engines"<sup id="cite_ref-killing_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-killing-57">[56]</a></sup> and, as of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Car&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, typically weigh between 1 and 3 tonnes.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup> Heavier cars are safer for the driver from a crash perspective, but more dangerous for other vehicles and road users.<sup id="cite_ref-killing_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-killing-57">[56]</a></sup> The weight of a car influences fuel consumption and performance, with more weight resulting in increased fuel consumption and decreased performance. The <a href="/wiki/SmartFortwo" class="mw-redirect" title="SmartFortwo">SmartFortwo</a>, a small <a href="/wiki/City_car" class="mw-redirect" title="City car">city car</a>, weighs 750–795&nbsp;kg (1,655–1,755&nbsp;lb). Heavier cars include full-size cars, SUVs and extended-length SUVs like the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Suburban" title="Chevrolet Suburban">Suburban</a>. </p>
      <p>Some places tax heavier cars more: as well as improving pedestrian safety this can encourage manufacturers to use materials such as recycled <a href="/wiki/Aluminium" title="Aluminium">aluminum</a> instead of steel.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup> In some competitions such as the <a href="/wiki/Eco-marathon" class="mw-redirect" title="Eco-marathon">Shell Eco Marathon</a>, average car weights of 45&nbsp;kg (99&nbsp;lb) have also been achieved.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup> These cars are only single-seaters (still falling within the definition of a car, although 4-seater cars are more common), but they nevertheless demonstrate the amount by which car weights could still be reduced, and the subsequent lower fuel use (i.e. up to a fuel use of 2560&nbsp;km/l).<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Seating_and_body_style">Seating and body style</span></h2> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Car_body_style" title="Car body style">Car body style</a>, <a href="/wiki/Car_classification" title="Car classification">Car classification</a>, <a href="/wiki/Truck_classification" title="Truck classification">Truck classification</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_size_class" title="Vehicle size class">Vehicle size class</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Most cars are designed to carry multiple occupants, often with four or five seats. Cars with five seats typically seat two passengers in the front and three in the rear. <a href="/wiki/Full-size_car" title="Full-size car">Full-size cars</a> and large <a href="/wiki/Sport_utility_vehicle" title="Sport utility vehicle">sport utility vehicles</a> can often carry six, seven, or more occupants depending on the arrangement of the seats. On the other hand, <a href="/wiki/Sports_car" title="Sports car">sports cars</a> are most often designed with only two seats. The differing needs for passenger capacity and their luggage or cargo space has resulted in the availability of a large variety of body styles to meet individual consumer requirements that include, among others, the <a href="/wiki/Sedan_(automobile)" title="Sedan (automobile)">sedan/saloon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hatchback" title="Hatchback">hatchback</a>, <a href="/wiki/Station_wagon" title="Station wagon">station wagon</a>/estate, and <a href="/wiki/Minivan" title="Minivan">minivan</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Safety">Safety</span></h2> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Car_safety" class="mw-redirect" title="Car safety">Car safety</a>, <a href="/wiki/Traffic_collision" title="Traffic collision">Traffic collision</a>, <a href="/wiki/Low_speed_vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Low speed vehicle">Low speed vehicle</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Epidemiology_of_motor_vehicle_collisions" title="Epidemiology of motor vehicle collisions">Epidemiology of motor vehicle collisions</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Car_crash_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Car_crash_2.jpg/220px-Car_crash_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Car_crash_2.jpg/330px-Car_crash_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Car_crash_2.jpg/440px-Car_crash_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Car_crash_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Result of a serious car collision
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Traffic collisions are the largest cause of injury-related deaths worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-who_stats_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-who_stats-12">[12]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mary_Ward_(scientist)" title="Mary Ward (scientist)">Mary Ward</a> became one of the first documented car fatalities in 1869 in <a href="/wiki/Birr,_County_Offaly" title="Birr, County Offaly">Parsonstown</a>, Ireland,<sup id="cite_ref-ward_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ward-62">[61]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Henry_Bliss_(road_accident_victim)" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry Bliss (road accident victim)">Henry Bliss</a> one of the United States' first pedestrian car casualties in 1899 in New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-bliss_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bliss-63">[62]</a></sup> There are now standard tests for safety in new cars, such as the <a href="/wiki/EuroNCAP" class="mw-redirect" title="EuroNCAP">EuroNCAP</a> and the US NCAP tests,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> and insurance-industry-backed tests by the <a href="/wiki/Insurance_Institute_for_Highway_Safety" title="Insurance Institute for Highway Safety">Insurance Institute for Highway Safety</a> (IIHS).<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Costs_and_benefits">Costs and benefits</span></h2> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economics_of_car_usage" class="mw-redirect" title="Economics of car usage">Economics of car usage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Car_costs" title="Car costs">Car costs</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_the_car_on_societies" title="Effects of the car on societies">Effects of the car on societies</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Chang%27an_avenue_in_Beijing.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Chang%27an_avenue_in_Beijing.jpg/220px-Chang%27an_avenue_in_Beijing.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Chang%27an_avenue_in_Beijing.jpg/330px-Chang%27an_avenue_in_Beijing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Chang%27an_avenue_in_Beijing.jpg/440px-Chang%27an_avenue_in_Beijing.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="750"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Chang%27an_avenue_in_Beijing.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Road_congestion" class="mw-redirect" title="Road congestion">Road congestion</a> is an issue in many major cities. (pictured is <a href="/wiki/Chang%27an_Avenue" title="Chang'an Avenue">Chang'an Avenue</a> in <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-66">[65]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The costs of car usage, which may include the cost of: acquiring the vehicle, repairs and <a href="/wiki/Auto_maintenance" class="mw-redirect" title="Auto maintenance">auto maintenance</a>, fuel, <a href="/wiki/Depreciation" title="Depreciation">depreciation</a>, driving time, <a href="/wiki/Parking_fee" class="mw-redirect" title="Parking fee">parking fees</a>, taxes, and insurance,<sup id="cite_ref-racv_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-racv-11">[11]</a></sup> are weighed against the cost of the alternatives, and the value of the benefits&nbsp;– perceived and real&nbsp;– of vehicle usage. The benefits may include on-demand transportation, mobility, independence and convenience,<sup id="cite_ref-setright_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-setright-13">[13]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Emergency_power_system" title="Emergency power system">emergency power</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> During the 1920s, cars had another benefit: "[c]ouples finally had a way to head off on unchaperoned dates, plus they had a private space to snuggle up close at the end of the night."<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Similarly the costs to society of car use may include; <a href="/wiki/Maintaining_road" class="mw-redirect" title="Maintaining road">maintaining roads</a>, <a href="/wiki/Land_use" title="Land use">land use</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air pollution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Road_congestion" class="mw-redirect" title="Road congestion">road congestion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">public health</a>, health care, and of disposing of the vehicle at the end of its life; and can be balanced against the value of the benefits to society that car use generates. Societal benefits may include: economy benefits, such as job and wealth creation, of car production and maintenance, transportation provision, society wellbeing derived from leisure and travel opportunities, and revenue generation from the <a href="/wiki/Category:Vehicle_taxes" title="Category:Vehicle taxes">tax</a> opportunities. The ability of humans to move flexibly from place to place has far-reaching implications for the nature of societies.<sup id="cite_ref-parking_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parking-14">[14]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_effects">Environmental effects</span></h2> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Exhaust_gas" title="Exhaust gas">Exhaust gas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waste_tires" class="mw-redirect" title="Waste tires">Waste tires</a>, <a href="/wiki/Environmental_effects_of_transport" title="Environmental effects of transport">Environmental effects of transport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motor_vehicle_emissions_and_pregnancy" title="Motor vehicle emissions and pregnancy">Motor vehicle emissions and pregnancy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Noise_pollution" title="Noise pollution">Noise pollution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Environmental_aspects_of_the_electric_car" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental aspects of the electric car">Environmental aspects of the electric car</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_recycling" title="Vehicle recycling">Vehicle recycling</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Externalities_of_automobiles" title="Externalities of automobiles">Externalities of automobiles</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vehicles_map_2001-2007.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Vehicles_map_2001-2007.gif/290px-Vehicles_map_2001-2007.gif" decoding="async" width="290" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Vehicles_map_2001-2007.gif/435px-Vehicles_map_2001-2007.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Vehicles_map_2001-2007.gif/580px-Vehicles_map_2001-2007.gif 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="359"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vehicles_map_2001-2007.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Vehicles in use per country from 2001 to 2007. It shows the significant growth in <a href="/wiki/BRIC" title="BRIC">BRIC</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Cars are a major cause of urban <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air pollution</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> with all types of cars producing dust from brakes, tyres and road wear.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> As of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Car&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the average diesel car has a worse effect on <a href="/wiki/Air_quality" class="mw-redirect" title="Air quality">air quality</a> than the average gasoline car.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> But both gasoline and diesel cars pollute more than electric cars.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup> While there are different ways to power cars most rely on <a href="/wiki/Gasoline" title="Gasoline">gasoline</a> or <a href="/wiki/Diesel_fuel" title="Diesel fuel">diesel</a>, and they consume almost a quarter of world oil production as of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Car&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-IEA2019_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IEA2019-45">[45]</a></sup> In 2018 passenger road vehicles emitted 3.6 <a href="/wiki/Gigatonne" class="mw-redirect" title="Gigatonne">gigatonnes</a> of carbon dioxide.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Car&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, due to greenhouse gases emitted during battery production, electric cars must be driven tens of thousands of kilometers before their lifecycle carbon emissions are less than fossil fuel cars:<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> but this is expected to improve in future due to longer lasting<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> batteries being produced in larger factories,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> and lower carbon electricity. Many governments are using fiscal policies, such as <a href="/wiki/Road_tax" title="Road tax">road tax</a>, to discourage the purchase and use of more polluting cars;<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> and many cities are doing the same with <a href="/wiki/Low-emission_zone" title="Low-emission zone">low-emission zones</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-78">[77]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fuel_tax" title="Fuel tax">Fuel taxes</a> may act as an incentive for the production of more efficient, hence less polluting, car designs (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_vehicles" class="mw-redirect" title="Hybrid vehicles">hybrid vehicles</a>) and the development of <a href="/wiki/Alternative_fuel" title="Alternative fuel">alternative fuels</a>. High fuel taxes or cultural change may provide a strong incentive for consumers to purchase lighter, smaller, more <a href="/wiki/Fuel-efficient" class="mw-redirect" title="Fuel-efficient">fuel-efficient</a> cars, or to <a href="/wiki/Car-free_movement" title="Car-free movement">not drive</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-78">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Car_longevity" title="Car longevity">lifetime of a car</a> built in the 2020s is expected to be about 16 years, or about 2 million kilometres (1.2 million miles) if driven a lot.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Energy_Agency" title="International Energy Agency">International Energy Agency</a> fuel economy improved 0.7% in 2017, but an annual improvement of 3.7% is needed to meet the Global Fuel Economy Initiative 2030 target.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> The increase in sales of SUVs is bad for fuel economy.<sup id="cite_ref-IEA2019_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IEA2019-45">[45]</a></sup> Many cities in Europe, have <a href="/wiki/Low-emission_zone" title="Low-emission zone">banned older fossil fuel cars</a> and all fossil fuel vehicles will be banned in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> from 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> Many Chinese cities limit licensing of fossil fuel cars,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> and many countries plan to stop selling them between 2025 and 2050.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The manufacture of vehicles is resource intensive, and many manufacturers now report on the environmental performance of their factories, including energy usage, <a href="/wiki/Waste" title="Waste">waste</a> and <a href="/wiki/Water_consumption" class="mw-redirect" title="Water consumption">water consumption</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> Manufacturing each kWh of battery emits a similar amount of carbon as burning through one full tank of gasoline.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup> The growth in popularity of the car allowed cities to <a href="/wiki/Urban_sprawl" title="Urban sprawl">sprawl</a>, therefore encouraging more travel by car resulting in inactivity and <a href="/wiki/Obesity" title="Obesity">obesity</a>, which in turn can lead to increased risk of a variety of diseases.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Animals and plants are often negatively affected by cars via <a href="/wiki/Habitat_destruction" title="Habitat destruction">habitat destruction</a> and pollution. Over the lifetime of the average car the "loss of habitat potential" may be over 50,000&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup> (540,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;ft) based on <a href="/wiki/Primary_production" title="Primary production">primary production</a> correlations.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> Animals are also killed every year on roads by cars, referred to as <a href="/wiki/Roadkill" title="Roadkill">roadkill</a>. More recent road developments are including significant environmental mitigation in their designs, such as green bridges (designed to allow <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_crossing" title="Wildlife crossing">wildlife crossings</a>) and creating <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_corridor" title="Wildlife corridor">wildlife corridors</a>. </p>
      <p>Growth in the popularity of vehicles and <a href="/wiki/Commuting" title="Commuting">commuting</a> has led to <a href="/wiki/Traffic_congestion" title="Traffic congestion">traffic congestion</a>. <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bogota" class="mw-redirect" title="Bogota">Bogota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sao_Paulo" class="mw-redirect" title="Sao Paulo">Sao Paulo</a> were the world's most congested cities in 2018 according to INRIX, a data analytics company.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Emerging_car_technologies">Emerging car technologies</span></h2> 
      <p>Although intensive development of conventional <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_vehicle" title="Battery electric vehicle">battery electric vehicles</a> is continuing into the 2020s,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup> other car <a href="/wiki/Propulsion" title="Propulsion">propulsion</a> technologies that are under development include <a href="/wiki/Wheel_hub_motor" title="Wheel hub motor">wheel hub motors</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Inductive_charging#Electric_vehicles" title="Inductive charging">wireless charging</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_car" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydrogen car">hydrogen cars</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup> and hydrogen/electric hybrids.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> Research into alternative forms of power includes using <a href="/wiki/Ammonia" title="Ammonia">ammonia</a> instead of hydrogen in <a href="/wiki/Fuel_cell" title="Fuel cell">fuel cells</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>New materials which may replace steel car bodies include aluminum,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fiberglass" title="Fiberglass">fiberglass</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carbon_fiber" class="mw-redirect" title="Carbon fiber">carbon fiber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biocomposite" title="Biocomposite">biocomposites</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Carbon_nanotube" title="Carbon nanotube">carbon nanotubes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Telematics" title="Telematics">Telematics</a> technology is allowing more and more people to share cars, on a <a href="/wiki/City_Car_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="City Car Club">pay-as-you-go</a> basis, through <a href="/wiki/Car_share" class="mw-redirect" title="Car share">car share</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carpool" title="Carpool">carpool</a> schemes. Communication is also evolving due to <a href="/wiki/Connected_car" title="Connected car">connected car</a> systems.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Autonomous_car">Autonomous car</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_car" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous car">Autonomous car</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-Expand_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">

         <td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31"></a></td>

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hands-free_Driving.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Hands-free_Driving.jpg/220px-Hands-free_Driving.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Hands-free_Driving.jpg/330px-Hands-free_Driving.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Hands-free_Driving.jpg/440px-Hands-free_Driving.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4974" data-file-height="3564"></a>

        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Fully autonomous vehicles, also known as driverless cars, already exist in prototype (such as the <a href="/wiki/Google_driverless_car" class="mw-redirect" title="Google driverless car">Google driverless car</a>), but have a long way to go before they are in general use.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Open_source_development">Open source development</span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Open_source_car" class="mw-redirect" title="Open source car">Open source car</a>
      </div> 
      <p>There have been several projects aiming to develop a car on the principles of <a href="/wiki/Open_design" class="mw-redirect" title="Open design">open design</a>, an approach to designing in which the plans for the machinery and systems are publicly shared, often without monetary compensation. None of the projects have succeeded in developing a car as a whole including both hardware and software, and no mass production ready open-source based designs have been introduced. Some car <a href="/wiki/Hacker_(programmer_subculture)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hacker (programmer subculture)">hacking</a> through <a href="/wiki/On-board_diagnostics" title="On-board diagnostics">on-board diagnostics</a> (OBD) has been done so far.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Car_sharing">Car sharing</span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Carsharing" title="Carsharing">Car-share</a> arrangements and <a href="/wiki/Carpool" title="Carpool">carpooling</a> are also increasingly popular, in the US and Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> For example, in the US, some car-sharing services have experienced double-digit growth in revenue and membership growth between 2006 and 2007. Services like car sharing offering a residents to "share" a vehicle rather than own a car in already congested neighborhoods.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry">Industry</span></h2> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry" title="Automotive industry">Automotive industry</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-Expand_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31"></a></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section <b>needs expansion</b>. You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Car&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>. <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2019</span>)</i></span>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Geely_assembly_line_in_Beilun,_Ningbo.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Geely_assembly_line_in_Beilun%2C_Ningbo.JPG/220px-Geely_assembly_line_in_Beilun%2C_Ningbo.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Geely_assembly_line_in_Beilun%2C_Ningbo.JPG/330px-Geely_assembly_line_in_Beilun%2C_Ningbo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Geely_assembly_line_in_Beilun%2C_Ningbo.JPG/440px-Geely_assembly_line_in_Beilun%2C_Ningbo.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Geely_assembly_line_in_Beilun,_Ningbo.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A car being assembled in a factory
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The automotive industry designs, develops, manufactures, markets, and sells the world's <a href="/wiki/Motor_vehicle" title="Motor vehicle">motor vehicles</a>, more than three-quarters of which are cars. In 2020 there were 56 million cars manufactured worldwide,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup> down from 67 million the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry_in_China" title="Automotive industry in China">automotive industry in China</a> produces by far the most (20 million in 2020), followed by Japan (7 million), then Germany, South Korea and India.<sup id="cite_ref-OICA2018_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OICA2018-104">[103]</a></sup> The largest market is China, followed by the USA. </p>
      <p>Around the world there are about a billion cars on the road;<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup> they burn over a trillion liters of gasoline and diesel fuel yearly, consuming about 50 <a href="/wiki/Exajoule" class="mw-redirect" title="Exajoule">EJ</a> (nearly 300 <a href="/wiki/Terawatt-hour" class="mw-redirect" title="Terawatt-hour">terawatt-hours</a>) of energy.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> The numbers of cars are increasing rapidly in China and India.<sup id="cite_ref-plunkettresearch.com_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plunkettresearch.com-15">[15]</a></sup> In the opinion of some, urban transport systems based around the car have proved unsustainable, consuming excessive energy, affecting the health of populations, and delivering a declining level of service despite increasing investment. Many of these negative effects fall disproportionately on those social groups who are also least likely to own and drive cars.<sup id="cite_ref-health_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-health-107">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FIA2018_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIA2018-108">[107]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_transport" title="Sustainable transport">sustainable transport</a> movement focuses on solutions to these problems. The car industry is also facing increasing competition from the public transport sector, as some people re-evaluate their private vehicle usage. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternatives">Alternatives</span></h2> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Alternatives_to_car_use" title="Alternatives to car use">Alternatives to car use</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Place_de_la_R%C3%A9publique_(Paris),_r%C3%A9am%C3%A9nagement,_2012-04-05_39.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Place_de_la_R%C3%A9publique_%28Paris%29%2C_r%C3%A9am%C3%A9nagement%2C_2012-04-05_39.jpg/220px-Place_de_la_R%C3%A9publique_%28Paris%29%2C_r%C3%A9am%C3%A9nagement%2C_2012-04-05_39.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Place_de_la_R%C3%A9publique_%28Paris%29%2C_r%C3%A9am%C3%A9nagement%2C_2012-04-05_39.jpg/330px-Place_de_la_R%C3%A9publique_%28Paris%29%2C_r%C3%A9am%C3%A9nagement%2C_2012-04-05_39.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Place_de_la_R%C3%A9publique_%28Paris%29%2C_r%C3%A9am%C3%A9nagement%2C_2012-04-05_39.jpg/440px-Place_de_la_R%C3%A9publique_%28Paris%29%2C_r%C3%A9am%C3%A9nagement%2C_2012-04-05_39.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Place_de_la_R%C3%A9publique_(Paris),_r%C3%A9am%C3%A9nagement,_2012-04-05_39.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A9lib%27" title="Vélib'">Vélib'</a> in Paris, France is the largest bikesharing system outside China<sup id="cite_ref-Access2011_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Access2011-109">[108]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Established alternatives for some aspects of car use include <a href="/wiki/Public_transport" title="Public transport">public transport</a> such as buses, <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">trolleybuses</a>, trains, <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">subways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tram_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Tram system">tramways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">light rail</a>, cycling, and <a href="/wiki/Walking" title="Walking">walking</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bicycle_sharing_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Bicycle sharing system">Bicycle sharing systems</a> have been established in China and many European cities, including <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>. Similar programs have been developed in large US cities.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup> Additional individual modes of transport, such as <a href="/wiki/Personal_rapid_transit" title="Personal rapid transit">personal rapid transit</a> could serve as an alternative to cars if they prove to be socially accepted.<sup id="cite_ref-asphalt_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asphalt-112">[111]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_meanings">Other meanings</span></h2> 
      <p>The term <i>motorcar</i> was formerly also used in the context of electrified rail systems to denote a car which functions as a small locomotive but also provides space for passengers and baggage. These locomotive cars were often used on suburban routes by both interurban and intercity railroad systems.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup> </p>
